<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="fcd1e9ba874b4f928e70005a43e21b9d"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="fcd1e9ba874b4f928e70005a43e21b9d">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'da5fbbe3-f5ed-4469-b5d1-60b6cc57a8d0'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        (function() {
            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {
                var store_domain = 'https://advanced.onlinelibrary.wiley.com';
                var session_id = 'D76A74D21F602B08017847F029D5E459';
                var url = ('https:' == document.location.protocol ? 'https://' : 'http://')
                    + "beacon.riskified.com?shop=" + store_domain + "&sid=" + session_id;
                var s = document.createElement('script');
                s.type = 'text/javascript';
                s.async = true;
                s.src = url;
                var x = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
                x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
            }
            if (window.attachEvent)
                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else
                window.addEventListener('load', riskifiedBeaconLoad, false);
        })();

                        <li class="sm-account__item"><a target="_blank" class="sm-account__link" href="https://orcid.org/0000-0002-8324-4160"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-orcid"></i><span>orcid.org/0000-0002-8324-4160</span></a></li>
                     </ul>
                     <p>School of Chemistry and Chemical Engineering, Shandong University, Jinan, 250100 China</p>
                     <p>E-mail: <a class="corr-email" title="Link to email address" href="mailto:shjlei@ncu.edu.cn"><span>shjlei@ncu.edu.cn</span></a>; <a class="corr-email" title="Link to email address" href="mailto:chexsl@sdu.edu.cn"><span>chexsl@sdu.edu.cn</span></a></p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Xiong/Shenglin">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span></div>
         </div>
      </div>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d413123448" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Metal thiophosphite has demonstrated promising application potential as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries. Nevertheless, the intrinsic low electrical conductivity and drastic volume expansion impede its commercialization. Herein, a series of metal thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> (metal = Fe, Ni, Co, and Cd) composites are constructed via Lewis acidic molten salt etching followed by synchronous phospho-sulfurization. The Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> substrate endows the thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrids with high electrical conductivity. Importantly, thiophosphite grown on the MXene layers exhibits a 3D cross-linked structure, which not only facilitates electron/ion transport, but also maintains robust structural stability owing to the space confinement effect. As a proof of concept, FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> demonstrates remarkable rate performance (827.4 and 598.1 mAh g<sup>1</sup> at 0.1 and 10 A g<sup>1</sup>, respectively) along with long-term cycling stability (capacity retention of 93.7% after 2000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>1</sup>). Impressively, the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub>//NVPO full cell exhibits a high reversible capacity of 396.8 mAh g<sup>1</sup> over 1350 cycles at 2 A g<sup>1</sup>. The sodium storage mechanism of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode is further unveiled through in situ XRD/ex situ HRTEM characterizations and theoretical calculations. This work provides a fresh perspective on enhancing the electrochemical performance of thiophosphite through the in situ construction of thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrids.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202407740-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202407740-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) offer lower material costs and more resource availability relative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), thereby endowing them with greater potential in the realm of energy storage. Moreover, SIBs exhibit comparable electrochemical performance to LIBs counterparts, providing a reliable solution for sustainable energy transformation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0001_R_d413123145e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Adv. Energy Mater.">1</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0002_R_d413123145e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - NanoMicro Lett.">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, their practical applications are plagued by the sluggish energy storage kinetics stemming from the larger Na<sup>+</sup> ion radius (0.98  vs 0.76  of Li<sup>+</sup>), leading to poor cyclability and inferior rate capability so far. The advancement of innovative high-performance anode materials is crucial in driving SIBs commercialization. In recent years, metal thiophosphites (metal = Fe, Ni, Co, Cd, Mn, Cu, etc.) have emerged as novel research hotspots for SIB anode materials in view of their appealing features.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0003_R_d413123145e510" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">3</a>-<a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0014_R_d413123145e510" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Specifically, the spacious van der Waals gap offers an ideal structure for the insertion and extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> ions. Additionally, the consecutive conversion reactions of P and S to Na ions result in theoretical capacities surpassing 1300 mAh g<sup>1</sup>, along with the improved rate and cycling performance. Unfortunately, the intrinsic low electrical conductivity and substantial volume expansion during charging and discharging processes lead to unsatisfactory rate and cycling capability of thiophosphite anodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0003_R_d413123145e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">3</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0005_R_d413123145e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem. Eng. J.">5</a>-<a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0007_R_d413123145e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Chem. Eng. J.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Considering these difficulties, strategies such as composite construction, size reduction, vacancy engineering, and interlayer modulation, have been implemented to tackle the inherent shortcomings of thiophosphites.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0005_R_d413123145e527" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem. Eng. J.">5</a>-<a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e527" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Among these, the design of composites is the most frequently employed. Incorporating conductive substrates such as Ndoped carbon,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0005_R_d413123145e532" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem. Eng. J.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> carbon nanotubes,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0008_R_d413123145e537" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0009_R_d413123145e537" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Chem. Eng. J.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and expanded graphite<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e543" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> not only enhances the conductivity of thiophosphites but also circumvents volume expansion. Since the discovery of MXene in 2011,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0015_R_d413123145e548" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Adv. Mater.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> composite designs involving MXene have been effectively utilized to improve the energy storage performance of various electrode materials, such as metal sulfides,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0016_R_d413123145e554" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Energy Mater.">16</a>-<a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0019_R_d413123145e554" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - ACS Nano">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> metal oxides,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0020_R_d413123145e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - New J. Chem.">20</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0021_R_d413123145e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - J. Mater. Chem. A">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and phosphorene.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0022_R_d413123145e564" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - eScience">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The research upsurge of using MXene as a substrate to fabricate highperformance composite electrodes is driven by its exceptional characteristics, including high electrical conductivity (typically 60008000 S cm<sup>1</sup>, reaching up to 2.4  10<sup>4</sup> S cm<sup>1</sup> for Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>), tunable surface chemistry, and 2D layered structure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0023_R_d413123145e584" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Adv. Mater.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Despite the excellent physicochemical properties of MXene, there have been few reports, to our knowledge, on the composite structure of thiophosphite with MXene, especially in the field of energy storage applications. In the limited research reports available, the preparation process of thiophosphite/MXene composite materials is highly tedious. This process involves the laborious preparation of MXene and the mechanical exfoliation of thiophosphite bulk materials, followed by their subsequent mixing and composite formation. Even more concerning is the fact that the preparation process of MXene is hazardous involving the use of toxic HF acid, and is time-consuming taking over 24&nbsp;h. Thus, it is imperative and challenging to develop an efficient, straightforward, and eco-friendly method for the preparation of thiophosphite/MXene composites. Furthermore, the development of novel thiophosphite/MXene composites and the comprehensive investigation into their sodium energy storage kinetics and underlying energy storage mechanisms are crucial.</p>
         
         <p>Unlike the conventional wet chemical etching method utilizing HF/bifluoride salts/alkali solutions as etchants, a brandnew, safe, and environmentally friendly technique, known as Lewis acidic molten salts etching, was developed in 2019 to efficiently prepare MXene.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0024_R_d413123145e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">24</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0025_R_d413123145e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nat. Mater.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This approach not only eliminates the need for toxic reagents, but also significantly shortens the preparation time. An important point to note is that Lewis acidic molten salts etching imparts MXene with uniform terminations, such as Cl, Br, or I functional groups, which exhibit metallic-level conductivity. In contrast, F or OH terminated MXene prepared by traditional HF or alkali etching techniques typically demonstrates semiconductor behavior.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0024_R_d413123145e597" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">24</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0026_R_d413123145e597" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - ACS Nano">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> What's even more exciting is that MXene with uniformly and abundantly loaded metal particles can be obtained through the Lewis acidic molten salts etching route, which has recently been directly applied to electrode materials or served as a precursor for the preparation of high-performance MXene/metal sulfide heterostructure electrodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0016_R_d413123145e602" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Energy Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0017_R_d413123145e602" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - J. Mater. Chem. A.">17</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0025_R_d413123145e602" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nat. Mater.">25</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0027_R_d413123145e602" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Electrochim. Acta">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Enhanced conductivity, promoted electrolyte ion migration kinetics, and robust architectures collectively contribute to their outstanding energy storage performance. As far as we know, there have been no reports to date regarding the utilization of these metal-decorated MXenes as precursors for the synthesis of thiophosphite/MXene composite materials.</p>
         
         <p>Inspired by the above considerations, herein, we constructed a series of metal thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> (T = O and Cl, metal = Fe, Ni, Co, and Cd) hybrids by synchronously phospho-sulfurizing metal/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> obtained through Lewis acidic molten salts etching. The in situ growth of thiophosphite nanosheets on the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene layers results in a 3D cross-linked architecture, which not only shortens the diffusion path of sodium ions and accelerates electrolyte penetration, but also maintains high structural stability owing to the space confinement effect. Additionally, the conductive Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> substrate forms a robust and conductive pathway for electron/ion transfer, significantly enhancing transportation kinetics during electrochemical reactions. The synergistic effects between Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> and thiophosphite greatly contribute to the improved sodium storage performance of the prepared thiophosphite/MXene composite materials. As a demonstration, the unique FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid exhibits high specific capacity (827.4 mAh g<sup>1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>1</sup>), excellent rate capability (598.1 mAh g<sup>1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>1</sup>), and stable cycling performance (597.8 mAh g<sup>1</sup> after 2000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>1</sup>). A fullcell device constructed with the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode and the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVPO) cathode further demonstrates an extended cycle life. Moreover, in situ XRD and ex situ HRTEM characterizations systematically elucidate the sodium storage mechanism of the prepared FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode, while theoretical calculations reveal the reasons behind the enhanced electrochemical kinetics. This work successfully develops a series of innovative high-performance metal thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene anode materials, offering new avenues for the advancement of thiophosphite electrode materials, and consequently, promoting the development of advanced SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202407740-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202407740-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>The synthesis route of thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites is depicted in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1a</a>. In this work, Lewis acidic molten salt etching followed by simultaneous in situ phospho-sulfurization processes were employed to fabricate thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites. In contrast to the traditional wet chemical etching of MAX and subsequent complex blending processes through mechanical or liquid-phase mixing, the proposed strategy herein exhibits marked superiority with respect to both preparation efficiency and safety (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). Taking the synthesis of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite as an example, Fe particle-loaded Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene was prepared by annealing a mixture of Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> MAX, FeCl<sub>2</sub>4H<sub>2</sub>O and NaCl/KCl salts at 750&nbsp;C for 24&nbsp;h. During this etching process, Al atoms within the interlayer initially lose electrons to form Al<sup>3+</sup> cations, subsequently combining with Cl<sup></sup> anions to produce AlCl<sub>3</sub> gas at approximately 178&nbsp;C. Following this, the Fe<sup>2+</sup> cations capture electrons and transform them into Fe metal particles, which attach to the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> layers. Ultimately, the termination anions (Cl and O) can fix the exposed Ti atoms through electrostatic adsorption, forming Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> (T = Cl or O) MXene.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0024_R_d413123145e786" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">24</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0025_R_d413123145e786" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nat. Mater.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The obtained Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> was subjected to synchronous phospho-sulfurization treatment at 450&nbsp;C for 1&nbsp;h under vacuum conditions. During this process, those Fe particles loaded on the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene layers reacted chemically with the sublimated P/S mixed atmosphere, leading to the growth of abundant FePS<sub>3</sub> nanosheets on the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> layers. After that, the final product, namely FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, was obtained. The proposed preparation strategy for thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrids simultaneously meets the requirements of safety, efficiency, and environmental friendliness.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202407740-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3c511ec6-38a1-49e8-b024-64e57636bbd4/adfm202407740-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/3c511ec6-38a1-49e8-b024-64e57636bbd4/adfm202407740-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f8cecf9b-dcbc-4439-9ecd-9891866f6c50/adfm202407740-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3c511ec6-38a1-49e8-b024-64e57636bbd4/adfm202407740-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202407740-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202407740" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic illustration of the synthetic process of thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrids. b) XRD patterns of Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> MAX and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene samples. c) XRD patterns of the Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> samples. d) TGA curves of the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> samples in air atmosphere. ej) High-resolution XPS spectra of (e) Ti 2<i>p</i>, (f) Cl 2<i>p</i>, (g) O 1<i>s</i>, (h) Fe 2<i>p</i>, (i) P 2<i>p</i>, and (j) S 2<i>p</i>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The X-ray diffraction (XRD) test is utilized to identify the phase and structural information of the prepared products. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1b,c</a>, after the etching with FeCl<sub>2</sub>4H<sub>2</sub>O molten salt, two distinct diffraction peaks can still be observed in the Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> intermediate, located at 7.94 and 15.88, which can correspond to the (002) and (004) crystal planes of the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> phase. The Bragg diffraction angle of the (002) crystal plane of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> (7.92) experiences a shift toward a lower angle compared to that of the Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> MAX raw material (9.47), and the strong diffraction peak at 39.1 of Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> almost disappears (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1b</a>). The aforementioned results demonstrate the successful synthesis of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene and the expansion of interlayer spacing.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0028_R_d413123145e971" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Energy Environ. Sci.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, three new peaks appearing at 44.7, 65.0, and 82.3 are identified, which can be indexed to the characteristic (110), (200), and (211) planes of elemental Fe (JCPDS card No. 060696), indicating the formation of Fe metal. Following phospho-sulfurization treatment of Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, several prominent new characteristic peaks can be detected at 13.7, 27.7, 30.4, 35.4, 48.6, and 53.3, which perfectly correspond to the (001), (002), (130), (131), (202), and (060) planes of the monoclinic FePS<sub>3</sub> phase with a space group of C2/m (JCPDS card No. 330672), providing evidence for the transformation of Fe to FePS<sub>3</sub>. Besides, a weak (002) peak at 7.93 belonged to Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> also can be found in the XRD patterns of the as-prepared FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> sample (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1c</a>). The above XRD results indicate the successful fabrication of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid. After immersing the Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite in an HCl solution, the elimination of Fe metal particles can be verified through XRD analysis. The XRD patterns of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1b</a> reveal the absence of characteristic peaks of Fe, while the intact (002) and (004) peaks of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> are retained. This validates the successful preparation of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene via the safe and green molten salt etching method. XRD spectra for Co/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, Ni/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, Cd/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> samples are presented in Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1S3</a> (Supporting Information). Similarly, the characteristic peaks of CoPS (JCPDS card No. 270139), NiPS<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS card No. 78-0499), and CdPS<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS card No. 38-1006) can be clearly identified. The (002) characteristic peak, observed at 7.9, corresponds to the presence of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene, as evidenced by the XRD patterns of these thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> samples. These outcomes validate the extendibility of the proposed technique, involving Lewis acidic molten salt etching and subsequent synchronous in situ phospho-sulfurization, for the fabrication of thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites.</p>
         
         <p>Thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) is utilized to determine the weight percentage of thiophosphite within the thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid. The weight loss of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene primarily stems from the following oxidation reaction: Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> + 5O<sub>2</sub>  3TiO<sub>2</sub> + 2CO<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0029_R_d413123145e1160" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The TGA profiles depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1d</a> reveal a weight loss of 4.3% and 14.9% for the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> samples, respectively. After annealing the pure FePS<sub>3</sub> nanosheets sample at 800&nbsp;C in an air atmosphere, a single oxidation product FePO<sub>4</sub> (JCPDS card No. 29-0715) was obtained (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). Accordingly, it can be inferred that FePS<sub>3</sub> undergoes the following chemical reaction with oxygen under the elevated temperature: FePS<sub>3</sub> + 5O<sub>2</sub>  FePO<sub>4</sub> + 3SO<sub>2</sub>. The weight loss value of 17.5% for FePS<sub>3</sub> can be determined. Therefore, the mass percentage of FePS<sub>3</sub> in the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite can be estimated as 80.3%. Also, the proportions of NiPS<sub>3</sub>, CdPS<sub>3</sub>, and CoPS in the NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> samples are 74.2%, 70.8%, and 58.1%, respectively (for detail, see Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5S7</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) measurements are conducted to better understand the surface elements and chemical environment of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> product. XPS survey spectrum of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> sample indicates the presence of Ti, Cl, C, O, Fe, P, and S elements (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information). The prominent O signal suggests partial oxidation of MXene during the molten salt etching process, which is further evidenced by the presence of TiO bonds reflected in a pair of peaks (466.5/460.6&nbsp;eV) in the high-resolution spectrum of Ti 2<i>p</i> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1e</a>). This oxidation process may originate from the four crystalline water molecules present in FeCl<sub>2</sub>4H<sub>2</sub>O salt. Another prominent doublet peak of Ti 2<i>p</i>, centered at 465.7/460.1&nbsp;eV, is indicative of the TiCl bonds in Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0016_R_d413123145e1297" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Energy Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, the TiCl bonds can be also observed in the Cl 2<i>p</i> core-level spectrum at binding energies of 201.0 and 199.4&nbsp;eV (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1f</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0024_R_d413123145e1307" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The above results demonstrate that the as-prepared MXene can undergo termination with Cl and O groups during the molten salt etching process. This imparts acceptable metallic-level conductivity to the prepared Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> (T = Cl and O).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0023_R_d413123145e1320" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Adv. Mater.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, a notable peak at 455.4&nbsp;eV can be assigned to the TiC chemical bond in the [TiC<sub>6</sub>] octahedral core of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0030_R_d413123145e1335" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nano Energy">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the O 1<i>s</i> spectrum (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1g</a>), three peaks can be deconvoluted, which can be allotted to the surface CTiOH species (532.2&nbsp;eV), and the chemisorbed or physically adsorbed oxygen (531.6&nbsp;eV) and water (533.3&nbsp;eV) on the surface. The existence of FePS<sub>3</sub> in the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> sample is also confirmed by the high-resolution XPS spectra. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1h</a>, the XPS spectrum of Fe 2<i>p</i> reveals deconvoluted Fe 2<i>p</i><sub>3/2</sub> and Fe 2<i>p</i><sub>1/2</sub> peaks at 709.1/713.8&nbsp;eV and 722.4/729.6&nbsp;eV, respectively, closely corresponding to the Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> valence state.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e1374" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For P 2<i>p</i> signals, two splitting peaks of P 2<i>p</i><sub>3/2</sub> and P 2<i>p</i><sub>1/2</sub> located at 133.6 and 134.7&nbsp;eV are observed, implying the presence of PS bonds within the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>6</sub> units. In addition, a peak observed at 131.9&nbsp;eV can be attributed to the PP bonds (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1i</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0005_R_d413123145e1395" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem. Eng. J.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The S 2<i>p</i> XPS spectrum depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0001">1j</a> exhibits two fitting peaks positioned at 161.4 and 162.6&nbsp;eV, representing the S 2<i>p</i><sub>3/2</sub> and S 2<i>p</i><sub>1/2</sub> core levels, respectively.</p>
         
         <p>The morphology and microstructure of the prepared samples are characterized by field-emission scanning electron microscopy (SEM), transmission electron microscopy (TEM), and high-resolution TEM (HRTEM). As illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9ac</a> (Supporting Information), the commercial Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> MAX exhibits a typical dense multilayer structure with a smooth surface. After subjecting MAX to molten salt etching with different salts, the interlayer spacing of Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, Ni/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, Cd/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and Co/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites is notably expanded (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0002">2ad</a>). The uniform distribution of Fe, Ni, Cd, and Co elements, as evidenced by the elemental mapping images, confirms that metal particles are uniformly loaded within the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> layers (Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10S13</a>, Supporting Information). This suggests that the molten salt etching technique is not only capable of successfully etching MAX, but also of anchoring the corresponding metal particles on MXene layers. After thorough immersion in concentrated HCl, the Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> sample exhibits a smooth surface and uniform distribution of elements Ti, Cl, and O (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9df</a>, Supporting Information), indicating the removal of metal particles and the generation of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> (T = Cl, O) MXene product. After subjecting the Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, Ni/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, Cd/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and Co/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites to synchronous phospho-sulfurization treatment, the metallic particles vanish, concomitant with the formation of thiophosphite nanosheets. These thiophosphite nanosheets are dispersed on the MXene surface in diverse orientations, forming a 3D cross-linked structure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0002">2eh</a>). This configuration offers an increased number of active sites and a shortened pathway for ion/electron transport, facilitating electrolyte infiltration. The HRTEM image of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene reveals a pronounced layered structure with a large lattice spacing of 1.09&nbsp;nm corresponding to the (002) crystal plane (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0002">2i</a>). The HRTEM image of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0002">2j</a> displays distinct lattice fringes with <i>d</i>-spacings of 1.09 and 0.25&nbsp;nm, corresponding to the (002) plane of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene and the (131) plane of FePS<sub>3</sub>, respectively. Additionally, a broad lattice fringe belonging to FePS<sub>3</sub> with an interplanar spacing of 0.64&nbsp;nm is also detected, suggesting the unique 2D layered structure of FePS<sub>3</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0002">2k</a>). Moreover, the selected area electron diffraction (SAED) patterns of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid reveal several clear diffraction rings, which can be ascribed to the (130) and (132) directions of FePS<sub>3</sub>, as well as the (004) and (008) directions of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0002">2l</a>). This provides further evidence of the successful construction of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid. The high-angle annular dark field (HAADF) elemental mapping images depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0002">2m</a> demonstrate the uniform distribution of Fe, P, S, Ti, Cl, C, and O elements within the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid. Similarly, the elemental mapping images of NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> prove the homogeneous dispersion of thiophosphite nanosheets on the MXene surface (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0002">2np</a>). For comparison, pure FePS<sub>3</sub> was synthesized by subjecting FeOOH nanoflowers (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information) to phospho-sulfurization. The monoclinic FePS<sub>3</sub> phase exhibits a 2D nanosheet morphology (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202407740-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/780e5648-b5db-4e21-97a7-3b8f02a28122/adfm202407740-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/780e5648-b5db-4e21-97a7-3b8f02a28122/adfm202407740-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/e8befcd6-b4f8-4ee3-8299-daeb5697a230/adfm202407740-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/780e5648-b5db-4e21-97a7-3b8f02a28122/adfm202407740-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202407740-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202407740" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">SEM images of a) Fe/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, b) Ni/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, c) Cd/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, d) Co/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, e) FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, f) NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, g) CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and h) CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> samples. i) HRTEM image of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> Mxene. j,k) HRTEM images, l) SAED image, and m) HAADF image and corresponding elemental mapping images of the prepared FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> sample. Elemental mapping images of n) CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, o) NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and p) CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To evaluate the sodium storage performance of the prepared thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, half-cells are assembled utilizing thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> as the anode electrode and sodium foil as the cathode electrode. As presented in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3a</a>, the initial three cycles of cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves for the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>1</sup> within the potential range of 0.013.0&nbsp;V demonstrate multiple oxidationreduction peaks occurring at different voltage stages. During the initial cathodic scan, a main peak observed at 1.57&nbsp;V is likely associated with the gradual sodiation of FePS<sub>3</sub> to generate the Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>S intermediates,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0011_R_d413123145e1821" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Small Methods">11</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0012_R_d413123145e1821" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - ACS Nano.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> while the shoulder peak that appears at 1.18&nbsp;V and disappears in subsequent cycles may be attributed to the irreversible rupture of PS bonds, leading to the formation of P and Na<sub>3</sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> products.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e1831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0031_R_d413123145e1831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - J. Mater. Chem. A">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The subsequent two broad peaks detected at 0.69 and 0.25&nbsp;V signify a multi-step sodiation process resulting in the formation of Na<sub>3</sub>P, Fe, and Na<sub>2</sub>S, as well as an irreversible reaction induced by the electrolyte decomposition.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e1841" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the reverse charging process, a distinct peak at 1.56&nbsp;V should originate from the desodiation of Na<sub>2</sub>S. The prominent peak at 2.07 is ascribed to a multistep desodiation process, leading to the formation of Na<sub>3</sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> and P. The subsequent CV profiles exhibit a close overlap, except for the first cycle, indicating a profoundly reversible electrochemical conversionalloying reaction process derived from Na<sub>3</sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> and P. It is worth mentioning that a pair of oxidationreduction peaks near 0&nbsp;V (0.04/0.08&nbsp;V) is detected in the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode, which also appears in the initial CV curves of the pure Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16a</a>, Supporting Information). The emergence of these extra oxidationreduction peaks is likely attributable to the insertion/extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> ions within the interlayers of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0032_R_d413123145e1887" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Nano Energy">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The CV curve profile of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode in the subsequent two cycles almost overlaps, indicating a high electrochemical repeatability. The initial CV curve of the pure FePS<sub>3</sub> electrode displays the oxidationreduction peaks akin to those observed in the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode, except for the absence of a pair of peaks near 0&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information). This suggests that both electrodes undergo comparable charge-discharge reaction processes.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202407740-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/bdaccf54-4ed3-48c7-a3eb-49b2b08d89c8/adfm202407740-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/bdaccf54-4ed3-48c7-a3eb-49b2b08d89c8/adfm202407740-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/14b600a1-311a-4788-a19b-525988228bdb/adfm202407740-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/bdaccf54-4ed3-48c7-a3eb-49b2b08d89c8/adfm202407740-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202407740-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202407740" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The initial CV curves of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>1</sup>. b) The initial GCD curves of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode at 0.05 A g<sup>1</sup>. c) Cycling performance at 1 A g<sup>1</sup> and d) rate performance of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, pure FePS<sub>3</sub>, and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes. e) GCD curves of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode at different current densities. f) Comparison diagram of specific capacity at 10 A g<sup>1</sup> between reported Febased SIBs anodes with asprepared FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode. g) Capacitive and diffusion contribution at different scan rates for FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode. h) Separation of the capacitive (shaded region) and diffusion currents at 1&nbsp;mV s<sup>1</sup>. i) GITT profiles and corresponding Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients after the activation process. j) Long-term cyclic performance and Coulombic efficiency of the three electrodes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The initial galvanostatic chargedischarge (GCD) curve of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode at 50&nbsp;mA g<sup>1</sup> is plotted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3b</a>. The initial discharge and charge-specific capacities of 1193 and 930 mAh g<sup>1</sup> are achieved, respectively, with an initial Coulombic efficiency of 77.9%. The initial capacity decay is primarily due to the irreversible electrochemical reactions and the formation of the SEI film. A reversible specific capacity of 780 mAh g<sup>1</sup> with a Coulombic efficiency approaching 100% is observed in the subsequent two GCD cycles, further confirming the highly reversible electrochemical sodium storage behavior. The cycling performance of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, FePS<sub>3</sub>, and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes is examined at a moderate current density of 1 A g<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;(Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3c</a>). The Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode demonstrates outstanding cycling longevity owing to its robust structural stability. It is notable that during the initial cycles, the specific capacity of both the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> and FePS<sub>3</sub> electrodes increases slowly, which is a common phenomenon observed in other reported 2D materials. This occurrence can be interpreted as a phenomenon known as the activation process, wherein more active sites are exposed due to the fracture of 2D nanosheets in the cycling process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e2083" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the subsequent cycling, the specific capacity of FePS<sub>3</sub> nanosheets experiences a drastic decline after 130 cycles, exhibiting a low retention rate of 56.9% after 500 cycles. After going through 500 continuous loops, the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite maintains a high specific capacity of 498 mAh g<sup>1</sup>, with an almost 100% capacity retention. The rate performance of these three electrodes is illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3d</a>. The specific capacity of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> is significantly higher than that of individual FePS<sub>3</sub> and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes at different current densities. For FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode, the high specific capacities of 828, 813, 801, 786, 755, 650, and 598 mAh g<sup>1</sup> can be achieved at 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10 A g<sup>1</sup>, respectively. When the current density returns to 0.1 A g<sup>1</sup>, the electrode still maintains a high specific capacity of 824 mAh g<sup>1</sup>, highlighting its outstanding rate capability. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3e</a>, the GCD curves of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode exhibit distinct chargedischarge plateaus even at a high current density of 10 A g<sup>1</sup>, providing compelling evidence of its exceptional rechargeability. The sloping CV curves of the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode show no voltage plateaus, indicating the pseudocapacitive-dominated electrochemical behavior (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16b</a>, Supporting Information). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3f</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information), even at a high current density of 10 A g<sup>1</sup>, the sodium storage specific capacity of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode surpasses that of other reported Fe-based anode materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e2187" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0016_R_d413123145e2187" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Energy Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0033_R_d413123145e2187" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Alloy. Compd.">33</a>-<a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0037_R_d413123145e2187" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Chem. Sci.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This indicates the remarkable rapid chargedischarge capability of the prepared FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid.</p>
         
         <p>To thoroughly elucidate the excellent rate capability of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode electrode, various electrochemical characterizations have been performed. Initially, the electrochemical energy storage kinetics are assessed through the equation: <i>i</i> = <i>av<sup>b</sup></i> (the <i>b</i>-values range between 0.5 and 1. A <i>b</i>-value close to 0.5 signifies a diffusion-dominated kinetic process, whereas a <i>b</i>-value approaching 1 indicates a surface Faradaic-dominated kinetic behavior).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e2227" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0038_R_d413123145e2227" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Nano Res.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Two significant peaks are chosen from Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a</a> (Supporting Information) to calculate the <i>b</i>-values, resulting in 0.95 and 0.89 for peak 1 and peak 2, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18b</a>, Supporting Information). These values surpass those obtained for the pure FePS<sub>3</sub> electrode, which are 0.89 and 0.81 (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19a,b</a>, Supporting Information). Then, the pseudocapacitive- and diffusion-controlled capacity contributions of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode are quantitatively calculated using the formula: <i>i</i>(<i>v</i>) = <i>k<sub>1</sub>v</i> + <i>k<sub>2</sub>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0012_R_d413123145e2272" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - ACS Nano.">12</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0039_R_d413123145e2272" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nano Res.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> where <i>v</i> and <i>i</i>(<i>v</i>) represent the scan rate and corresponding current, respectively, while <i>k<sub>1</sub>v</i> and <i>k<sub>2</sub>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> represent the currents associated with non-Faradaic and Faradaic behaviors, respectively. The capacitance contribution values of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode range from 81.7% to 94.6% at scan rates between 0.2 and 1&nbsp;mV s<sup>1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3g</a>), which is significantly higher than that of the pure FePS<sub>3</sub> electrode (64.5% to 80.1%) (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19c</a>, Supporting Information). As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3h</a>, the fitted CV curve at 1&nbsp;mV s<sup>1</sup> exhibits a high capacitance contribution of 94.6%, surpassing that of pure FePS<sub>3</sub> (80.1%) (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19d</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) characterization after activation is employed to calculate the Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Na+</sub>) of the prepared samples. As can be observed from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3i</a>, the plateaus of the discharge curves and the variation trend of D<sub>Na+</sub> with changing voltage are consistent for both the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> and FePS<sub>3</sub> anode electrodes. This observation suggests a similarity in their energy storage mechanisms. It is evident that during the sodiation process, the D<sub>Na+</sub> value of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> (11.2 10.7 cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>1</sup>) surpasses that of pure FePS<sub>3</sub> (12.0 10.9 cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>1</sup>), demonstrating the promoted Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics. The outstanding rate performance of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode should be attributed to the introduction of the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene conductive substrate, which enhances the conductivity of FePS<sub>3</sub>. This conclusion can be verified through the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) testing. The Nyquist plot comprises a semicircle in the high-frequency region and an inclined line in the low-frequency region. It is fitted using the equivalent circuit illustrated in the inset image of Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20a</a> (Supporting Information). Wherein, <i>R</i><sub>b</sub>, <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>, and <i>Z</i><sub>w</sub> denote the electrolyte resistance, charge transfer resistance, and Warburg impedance, respectively. The FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode exhibits an <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value of 2.7 , while the pure FePS<sub>3</sub> and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes display a higher <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of 12.5 and 6.3  (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20a</a>, Supporting Information), respectively. In addition, the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusivity is further assessed by linear fitting of the Z'<sup>1/2</sup> plot in the low-frequency region. The slope values for FePS<sub>3</sub>, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes are calculated as 9.75, 7.94, and 4.77, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20b</a>, Supporting Information). The small slope value for the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode indicates its rapid Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics, further explaining its outstanding electrochemical performance. Additionally, the 3D cross-linked structure of FePS<sub>3</sub> grown on the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> layer also provides rapid pathways for electron/ion transport.</p>
         
         <p>To further demonstrate the structural stability of the prepared FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite at high chargedischarge rates, a long-term cycling stability test is conducted at a high current density of 5 A g<sup>1</sup> after the activation process at 0.05 A g<sup>1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0003">3j</a>). The capacity of the pure FePS<sub>3</sub> anode electrode gradually diminishes with a relatively low retention rate of 71.2% after 1500 cycles. The Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode reveals a stable long-term cycling life at 2 A g<sup>1</sup>. After the in situ decoration of FePS<sub>3</sub> nanosheets on the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene substrate, the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite delivers a high specific capacity of 596 mAh g<sup>1</sup> after 2000 cycles, showing a negligible capacity degradation. Moreover, the coulombic efficiency of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode approaches 100% throughout the cycling process. The outstanding cycling performance can be attributed to both the robust structural stability of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> and the space confinement effect. To evaluate the electrochemical performance of the prepared materials in commercial carbonate-based electrolytes, 1&nbsp;M NaPF<sub>6</sub> solution in ethylene carbonate (EC) and dimethyl carbonate (DMC) with 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) is employed as the electrolytes. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a> (Supporting Information), the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode demonstrates markedly inferior rate capability and cycling stability in the carbonate-based electrolytes compared to its performance in the ether-based electrolyte (see Supporting Information for details).</p>
         
         <p>To validate the universality of the proposed preparation strategy and the excellent sodium storage performance of the prepared thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites, halfcells with NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, or CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> materials as the anode electrode and sodium foil as the cathode electrode are assembled, and their electrochemical performance is examined. The initial CV curves at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>1</sup> for the NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode electrodes are plotted in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0004">4ac</a>. In the initial cathodic scan for the NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode, the prominent peak at 2.18&nbsp;V may be attributed to the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> ions, leading to the formation of Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>NiPS<sub>3</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e2658" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0012_R_d413123145e2658" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - ACS Nano.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It can be seen that a sharp peak at 1.41&nbsp;V should be associated with the gradual sodiation of NiPS<sub>3</sub> as a result of forming Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>S intermediates. A shoulder peak located at 0.87&nbsp;V may correspond to the irreversible fracture of PS bonds to form P and Ni<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<i><sub>y</sub></i> species.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0013_R_d413123145e2675" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - J. Energy Chem.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the progression of sodiation, the observation of a broad peak at 0.52&nbsp;V implies a multi-step sodiation process of P and Ni<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<i><sub>y</sub></i>, resulting in the generation of Na<sub>3</sub>P, Ni, and Na<sub>2</sub>S, along with the irreversible reactions and the formation of SEI film.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e2691" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the initial charging process, a minor peak at 1.56&nbsp;V is indicative of the desodiation of Na<sub>2</sub>S.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0012_R_d413123145e2698" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - ACS Nano.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Afterward, two peaks sequentially emerge at 2.02 and 2.35&nbsp;V, signifying a multi-step desodiation process that results in the formation of Ni<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<i><sub>y</sub></i> and P (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0004">4a</a>). For the CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode electrode, during the initial sodiation process, a faint peak appears at 2.09&nbsp;V, likely associated with the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> ions to form Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>CoPS.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0040_R_d413123145e2726" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Energy Storage Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Two broad peaks appear at 0.79 and 0.34&nbsp;V, corresponding to the formation of reduction products Na<sub>3</sub>P, Na<sub>2</sub>S, and metallic Co, accompanied by the fracture of PS bonds and the gradual formation of SEI film at the electrode/electrolyte interface.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0008_R_d413123145e2736" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0041_R_d413123145e2736" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the charging process, two reduction peaks at 1.69 and 2.01&nbsp;V can be attributed to the reversible oxidation reactions, resulting in the formation of CoS<sub>2</sub> and elemental phosphorus (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0004">4b</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0008_R_d413123145e2746" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the initial discharge process for the CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode electrode, the peak at 1.48&nbsp;V may indicate the formation of Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>S intermediates. A weak peak centered at 1.07&nbsp;V may result from the irreversible fracture of PS bonds.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e2765" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0031_R_d413123145e2765" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - J. Mater. Chem. A">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Meanwhile, a sharp peak at 0.41&nbsp;V should be induced by the generation of Na<sub>3</sub>P, Na<sub>2</sub>S, and elemental Cd products, together with an irreversible side reaction (electrolyte decomposition and SEI film formation). In the following initial anodic sweep, three peaks are detected at 1.55, 1.95, and 2.46&nbsp;V, which may originate from the generation of oxidation products P and Cd<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<i><sub>y</sub></i> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0004">4c</a>). The subsequent two cycles of CV curve profiles for these three thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes show significant overlap, indicating excellent electrochemical reversibility. Similar to FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, the NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes derive their specific capacity collectively from both phosphorus and metal sulfides. It's noteworthy that all the fabricated thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes display an additional pair of oxidation/reduction peaks close to 0&nbsp;V, stemming from Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction within the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> interlayer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0032_R_d413123145e2845" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Nano Energy">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>

            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202407740-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/19fe4a86-a875-41e9-a947-bcbe145e2e1a/adfm202407740-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/19fe4a86-a875-41e9-a947-bcbe145e2e1a/adfm202407740-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/441a986d-a74f-4dc9-b697-9d43f681ce6d/adfm202407740-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/19fe4a86-a875-41e9-a947-bcbe145e2e1a/adfm202407740-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202407740-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202407740" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
