                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The initial CV curves of the fabricated a) NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, b) CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub>, and c) CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>1</sup>. d) The initial GCD curves of NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes at 0.05 A g<sup>1</sup>. e) Rate performance of NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes. f) Comparison of the rate performance of NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes with reported Ni(Co, Cd)based anodes for SIBs systems. g) Long-term cyclic performance and Coulombic efficiency of NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes at 5 A g<sup>1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The initial GCD curves of these three electrodes at 0.05 A g<sup>1</sup> within the voltage range of 0.013&nbsp;V are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a> (Supporting Information). The NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes display initial discharge/charge specific capacities of 1130/867, 1029/780, and 1138/893 mAh g<sup>1</sup>, respectively, along with initial Coulombic efficiencies of 76.7%, 75.8%, and 78.5%, respectively. The rate performance of these three electrodes is illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0004">4d,e</a>. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0004">4d</a>, all three electrodes display clear chargedischarge voltage plateaus, corresponding to the oxidationreduction peaks in the CV curves mentioned above. Even at high current densities, various voltage plateaus are still observable, demonstrating excellent rechargeable capability. The NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode delivers high specific capacities of 801, 788, 790, 779, 726, 669, and 596 mAh g<sup>1</sup> at current densities of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10 A g<sup>1</sup>, respectively. For the CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode, the considerable specific capacities of 636, 579, 567, 562, 551, 521, and 488 mAh g<sup>1</sup> can be achieved under the same current densities. Similarly, the reversible specific capacities of 679, 623, 603, 579, 513, 465, and 416 mAh g<sup>1</sup> can be yielded for the CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> sample. When the current density is reverted back to 0.1 A g<sup>1</sup>, the notable discharge-specific capacities of 877, 616, and 686 mAh g<sup>1</sup> can still be maintained for the NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes, respectively. The outstanding rate capability of these three electrodes outperforms or is comparable to the majority of reported Fe, Ni, or Co-based anode electrode materials applied in SIBs (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0004">4f</a>; Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0008_R_d413123145e3125" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0011_R_d413123145e3125" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Small Methods">11</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0016_R_d413123145e3125" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Energy Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0042_R_d413123145e3125" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">42</a>-<a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0047_R_d413123145e3125" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, all three electrodes exhibit stable cycling performance. High specific capacities of 653, 483, and 441 mAh g<sup>1</sup> are maintained even after 2000 GCD cycles at 5 A g<sup>1</sup>. Moreover, near 100% Coulombic efficiency during the cycling tests suggests the highly reversible electrochemical processes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0004">4g</a>). To further clarify the underlying reasons for the outstanding rate capability of the three electrodes, the kinetic processes in these electrodes are meticulously analyzed by distinguishing the contributions of the surfacecapacitive and iondiffusion behaviors (Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23S25</a>, Supporting Information). As presented in Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23a, S24a</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25a</a> (Supporting Information), two prominent peaks are chosen for evaluating the <i>b</i>-values related to the kinetic behavior. The NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes all demonstrate the <i>b</i>-values approaching 1, with respective values of 0.91/0.92, 0.91/0.84, and 0.75/0.79 (Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23b, S24b</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25b</a>, Supporting Information). Further validation of the rapid kinetic behavior of these electrodes is provided by the contribution rates of surface capacitance and ion diffusion. Specifically, the capacitance contribution rates of the fabricated NiPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, CoPS/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and CdPS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode electrodes range from 71.6% to 92.8%, 87.9% to 94.2%, and 69.1% to 92.5%, respectively, within a scan rate range of 0.21&nbsp;mV s<sup>1</sup> (Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23c, S24c</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25c</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">To comprehensively understand the sodium storage mechanism of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite, in situ XRD, and ex situ HRTEM, SAED measurements of the sodiation/desodiation reactions are conducted during the first GCD discharge/charge process. The in situ XRD patterns during the first cycle of chargedischarge are illustrated in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0005">5a</a>. Evidently, a distinct reflection of the BeO substrate is discernible at 38.6. In the initial open-circuit voltage state, three distinct diffraction peaks at 27.7, 30.4, and 35.5 correspond to the (002), (130), and (131) planes of the FePS<sub>3</sub> phase, respectively. As the discharge progresses to 1.6&nbsp;V, these three peaks of FePS<sub>3</sub> gradually fade, accompanied by the emergence of a diffraction peak located at 24.5 of Na<sub>3</sub>FeS<sub>3</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e3248" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As the discharge proceeds, this peak disappears, and new peaks emerge at 22.4 and 36.1, attributable to the (400) plane of Na<sub>2</sub>S and the (110) plane of Na<sub>3</sub>P, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0008_R_d413123145e3257" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0048_R_d413123145e3257" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - J. Mater. Chem. A">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the charging process, the peaks corresponding to Na<sub>2</sub>S and Na<sub>3</sub>P gradually diminish and eventually disappear upon reaching a fully charged state, while the peak of Na<sub>3</sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> at 24.5 reappears. In the state of complete charging, the absence of observable peaks for elemental P may stem from its amorphous characteristics and relatively small size.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0008_R_d413123145e3271" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0049_R_d413123145e3271" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Nano Energy">49</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0050_R_d413123145e3271" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - J. Mater. Chem. A">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It is worth noting that the peaks associated with the FePS<sub>3</sub> phase do not reappear in the fully desodiation state due to the irreversible rupture of PS bonds.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0005_R_d413123145e3279" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem. Eng. J.">5</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e3279" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> More significantly, the phase transformation of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> during the first sodiationdesodiation loop can also be verified by ex situ HRTEM and SAED measurements (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0005">5be</a>). Upon complete discharge to 0.01&nbsp;V, the resultant products display <i>d</i>-spacings of 0.340, 0.249, and 0.183&nbsp;nm, corresponding to the (220) plane of Na<sub>2</sub>S, the (110) plane of Na<sub>3</sub>P, and the (200) plane of metallic Fe, respectively. This indicates the occurrence of conversion and alloying reactions during the discharge process. A broad lattice spacing of 0.761&nbsp;nm is also observed, likely originating from the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> phase (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0005">5b</a>). Moreover, the distinct diffraction spots in the SAED patterns obtained in the fully charged state further validate the presence of Na<sub>2</sub>S, Na<sub>3</sub>P, and Fe phases (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0005">5c</a>). As the electrode is continuously charged to a state of 3.0&nbsp;V, two distinct lattice fringes with <i>d</i>-spacings of 0.208 and 0.331&nbsp;nm can be observed (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0005">5d</a>). These two lattice fringes should be ascribed to the (250) plane of the Na<sub>3</sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> phase and the (021) crystal plane of the P phase. The corresponding SAED patterns further corroborate the presence of Na<sub>3</sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> and P phases (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0005">5e</a>). Furthermore, the HAADFSTEM image and energydispersive X-ray (EDX) elemental mapping images presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0005">5f</a> illustrate the uniform distribution of Ti, Fe, P, S, and Na elements. This uniform distribution underscores the conversion reactions and the good structural stability of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite structure. These observations are highly consistent with the XRD results, further elucidating the sodium storage mechanism of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode. This storage mechanism can be visually represented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0005">5g</a>. Specifically, the following reaction equations can be employed to signify its reaction mechanism:

         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202407740-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/54e0faa1-c6a8-42f1-83d4-c2b8099f3d92/adfm202407740-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/54e0faa1-c6a8-42f1-83d4-c2b8099f3d92/adfm202407740-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/b73a4a32-9206-4bb9-9bb4-d5a7b0601d93/adfm202407740-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/54e0faa1-c6a8-42f1-83d4-c2b8099f3d92/adfm202407740-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202407740-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202407740" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) In situ XRD patterns of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode at different dischargecharge stages. b,d) HRTEM images and c,e) the corresponding SAED patterns of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> electrode after first discharging to 0.01&nbsp;V and charging to 3.0&nbsp;V. f) HAADF-STEM image, and elemental mapping images of Ti, Fe, P, S, and Na after first discharging to 0.01&nbsp;V. g) The schematic illustration of Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism for the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The density functional theory (DFT) calculations are conducted to enhance the understanding of why the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode exhibits superior Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance. The constructed computational models of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, FePS<sub>3</sub>, and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> are provided in Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26, S27</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a> (Supporting Information). According to the density of states (DOS) plots depicted in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0006">6ac</a> for Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, FePS<sub>3</sub>, and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, there is a discernible augmentation in electron density near the Fermi level within the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite configuration relative to pure FePS<sub>3</sub>. This observation implies a notable enhancement in the electronic conductivity of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>. The models illustrating sodium adsorption on Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, FePS<sub>3</sub>, and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0006">6d</a>. Evidently, with the incorporation of the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> substrate featuring an adsorption energy of 3.33&nbsp;eV, the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite manifests a notably reduced adsorption energy (2.98&nbsp;eV) in comparison to FePS<sub>3</sub> (2.71&nbsp;eV). The robust sodium adsorption capability of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> confers advantages for enhancing the Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity. Finally, it is observed that the Na<sup>+</sup> migration barrier within the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid (0.35&nbsp;eV) is significantly diminished in comparison to that within FePS<sub>3</sub> (0.43&nbsp;eV), as illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0006">6e</a>. This finding indicates that the incorporation of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> MXene facilitates the Na<sup>+</sup> ions diffusion. Thus, the combination of significantly enhanced electronic conductivity, elevated sodium adsorption energy, and reduced Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barrier collectively confers superior rate capability and cycling performance upon the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202407740-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/18bcb1ec-7bcc-43c2-8470-b0ca586937cc/adfm202407740-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/18bcb1ec-7bcc-43c2-8470-b0ca586937cc/adfm202407740-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/bf7459a7-4d8a-44cb-9721-a3d08209b678/adfm202407740-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/18bcb1ec-7bcc-43c2-8470-b0ca586937cc/adfm202407740-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202407740-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202407740" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Theoretical simulation of sodium adsorption/migration for FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrid: DOS plots (fermi levels are set as zero and indicated with dashed lines) of a) FePS<sub>3</sub>, b) Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and c) FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>. d) Top view and side view structures of sodium adsorption on FePS<sub>3</sub>, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and the corresponding adsorption energy. e) Migration energy barrier of Na<sup>+</sup> ion in FePS<sub>3</sub>, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>, and FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To assess the practical application potential of the prepared thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites, taking the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode material as an example, a full cell (FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub>//NVPO) is assembled using NVPO as the cathode electrode (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0007">7a</a>). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0007">7b</a>, the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>//NVPO full cell demonstrates acceptable specific capacities of 461, 429, 398, 378, and 340 mAh g<sup>1</sup> at 0.5, 1, 2, 3, and 5 A g<sup>1</sup>, respectively. Even when the current density returns to 0.5 A g<sup>1</sup>, a high specific capacity of 452 mAh g<sup>1</sup> is still maintained, implying the excellent rate capability of the full cell. The full-cell device delivers a maximum energy density of 323.2&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>1</sup> at a power density of 379.9&nbsp;W kg<sup>1</sup>. Even when the power density increases to 4372.5&nbsp;W kg<sup>1</sup>, a high energy density of 198.6&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>1</sup> is also maintained (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a>, Supporting Information). The amorphous NVPO with a layered structure exhibits excellent rate performance (106 and 83 mAh g<sup>1</sup> at 0.1 and 5 A g<sup>1</sup>, respectively) and stable cycling life with capacity retention rate close to 100% after 300 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>1</sup>) (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a>, Supporting Information). Surprisingly, the full cell still contributes a considerable capacity reaching 397 mAh g<sup>1</sup> even after suffering a very long cycle of 1350 loops at a high current density of 2 A g<sup>1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0007">7c</a>). In the inset panel of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0007">7c</a>, it can be found that the full cell exhibits consistent voltage plateaus in the GCD curves throughout various cycling periods. Remarkably, the cycling performance of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> stands out among the sodium-ion full-cell systems (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0007">7d</a>; Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0005_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem. Eng. J.">5</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0008_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0010_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0035_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nano Energy">35</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0036_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Nano Lett.">36</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0042_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">42</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0043_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - J. Energy Chem.">43</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0047_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">47</a>, <a href="#adfm202407740-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202407740-bib-0051_R_d413123145e3911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, an LED lamp labeled MTP with a 3.7&nbsp;V voltage can be illuminated by two 2025-type coin cells in a fully charged state (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202407740-fig-0007">7e</a>). These outstanding superiorities underscore the significant application potential of thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> hybrids in advanced energy storage fields.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202407740-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/219a9c56-ab16-4ff1-9196-dff2cfe268c7/adfm202407740-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/219a9c56-ab16-4ff1-9196-dff2cfe268c7/adfm202407740-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/173e1299-43fd-4975-b6de-126b872c257f/adfm202407740-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/219a9c56-ab16-4ff1-9196-dff2cfe268c7/adfm202407740-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202407740-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202407740" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic diagram of the assembled FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>//NVPO full cell. b) Rate performance of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>//NVPO full cell. c) Long-term cycling stability of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>//NVPO full cell over 1350 GCD cycles at 2 A g<sup>1</sup>. Inset: GCD curves recorded at different cycle numbers. d) A comparison of the cyclic performance of FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>//NVPO full cell with the previously reported full-cell systems. e) Digital photograph of LED panel powered by FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i>//NVPO full-battery.</div>
               </figcaption>

         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202407740-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202407740-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, a simple, safe, environmentally friendly, and novel method, involving Lewis molten salt etching followed by a synchronous phosphosulfurization process, has been developed to efficiently prepare thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites as SIBs anode materials. The thiophosphite nanosheets are insitu decorated on the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> surface to form a 3D cross-linked structure, which facilitates the electrolyte infiltration, riches the active sites, and shortens the ion diffusion pathway. The introduction of the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> substrate enhances the conductivity of thiophosphite and alleviates volume expansion during the sodiation/desodiation process. As an illustration, these positive effects collectively endow the thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composites with outstanding half-cell and full-cell sodium storage performance. In situ XRD and ex situ HRTEM characterizations reveal the energy storage mechanism of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> anode, involving the fracture of PS bonds to form P and Na<sub>3</sub>FeS<sub>3</sub>, collectively providing a significant specific capacity. Moreover, DFT calculations discover the stronger sodium adsorption capability, higher DOS near the Fermi level, and lower diffusion barrier of the FePS<sub>3</sub>/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<i><sub>x</sub></i> composite compared to pure FePS<sub>3</sub>. This work further expands the application scope of the Lewis molten salt etching method. Additionally, it provides a novel approach for the preparation of thiophosphite/Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub> composites as high-performance rechargeable battery anodes through Lewis molten salt etching followed by synchronous phospho-sulfurization treatment.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

      <section class="article-section article-section__supporting" data-suppl="/doi/suppl/10.1002/adfm.202407740?onlyLog=true">
